ORAL ANSWERS TO QUESTIONS

: :

TRAIN SERVICE TO NORTH : NUMBER OF TRIPS 0640/09 1. . . .

( ... ) (The Hon. R.P.A. Ranaweera Pathirana) - (1) : () (i) ; (ii) , ; ? () (i) ; (ii) , ; (iii) , ; ? () , ? () , ? :

() (i ) ,

( i i ) ? () (i ) , ( i i ) , , ( i ii ) , ? () ? () , ? asked the Minister of Transport:

(a) Will he inform this House -

(i) the name of the railway station up to which the trains could be operated beyond Anuradhapura due to the war situation that prevailed in the North; and

(ii) the name of the railway station up to which the trains were operated and the date on which it was done if the trains were operated beyond Vavuniya after the end of the war? (b) Will he submit to this House-

(i) whether a ceremony was held to mark the com-mencement of train services beyond Vavuniya;

(ii) if so, the date on which it was held; and (iii) the number of times that the trains were oper-ated in those railway lines on the same days in each month subsequent to the above mentioned ceremony? (c) Will he admit that even though a train service was started to the North, the number of trips are not sufficient to meet the needs of the transport re-quirement of the commuters? (d) If not, why? 183 30301 3,205,000 184 30401 5,013,000 185 30501 704,000 186 30601 202,340,000 187 30602 400,000,000 188 30701 9,888,000 189 30801 203,640,000 190 30901 7,802,000 191 31001 11,327,000 192 31002 40,000,000 193 31003 80,000,000 194 31101 5,410,000 195 32001 25,040,000 196 32201 3,614,000 197 32301 233,000 198 32401 696,000 6,222,467,000

That this Parliament resolves, -

(a) that during the period commencing on January 1, 2010 and ending on the day immediately preceding that the date of the coming into operation of the Appropriation Act, providing for the services of the financial year 2010 and ending on December 31, 2010, sums not exceeding Rupees three hun-dred and fifty six thousand four hundred and sixty five million five hundred and seven thousand (Rs. 356,465,507,000) shall be payable out of the Consolidated Fund of the Democratic Socialist Republic of Sri Lanka for the services specified in the First Schedule to this resolution, (being services in respect of which provision for expenditure was made by the Appropria-tion Act No. 43 of 2008 and by Supplementary Estimates) and that the said sums may be expended as specify in that Sched-ule; and

(b) sums not exceeding rupees six thousand two hundred and twenty two million four hundred and sixty seven thousand (Rs. 6,222,467,000) in the aggregate, shall be payable, by way of advances out of the Consolidated Fund of the Democratic Socialist Republic of Sri Lanka for the services specified in Column I of the Second Schedule to this Resolution and that the debits incurred in respect of any of such services during the aforesaid period, shall not exceed the maximum limits as are specified in the corresponding entry in Column II of that Schedule.

(Cabinet approval signified)

Ranil Wickremasinghe) , Article 75 of the Constitution states, I quote: Parliament shall have power to make laws, including laws having retrospective effect and repealing or amending any provision of the Constitution,.. So, the Constitution and laws stand to be operated. The Constitution has to stand together with the laws of the country. If you have brought an Appropriation Bill, you

could have said, two laws stood side by side. But, you have a Regulation. There is nothing in the Constitution which says that a Regulation overrides the law. So, you are violating the Constitution if you say that a Regulation is overriding the law. I am going according to - [Interruption.] ( ) (Mr. Speaker) ? [ ] ( ) (The Hon. There are four Ministers. ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake)

Yes, that is right. There are four Ministers and today, each is speechless even when we refer them to these matters. What has happened today? You have put the country into jeopardy. We managed that. The United National Party, when we were governing, was able to see the writing on the wall and obtain that benefit from the European Union. I was happy that the Hon. (Prof.) G.L. Peiris was with us working shoulder to shoulder to get the European Union to say, Yes, Sri Lanka deserves it. Unfortunately, the same brief has been passed on to him now to defend it, but taking an opposite stance on the basis that we have to implement our Constitution. Nobody should ever dare try to tell us what our country needs to do. I, as an Opposition Member, was the first to conform to that. But what has happened today? Your own Ministers and your own people are saying that there is external interference in internal affairs. What is the internal affair on which intrusion has taken place? You are breaching our own Constitution; you are breaching the rights of the media. The very application that you put forward is being violated by your own selves and then you have the audacity to turn round and say, Sorry, there is external intrusion into our local affairs. Look at what happened in Moratuwa; see what happened in Kaduwela; and see what happened in Bambalapitiya the other day. These are stark realities seen by the rest of the world. Let us all get together and protect our Constitution. That is all what is required. I just mentioned that because I saw my learned Friend, the Hon. (Prof.) G.L. - - . , . , -- . . . ; . . , , . ( ) (The Presiding Member) . ( ) (The Hon. (Prof.) Tissa Vitharana) . , , . , . . , . . , . "" , , . ( ) (The Presiding Member) , . . 10 . [. . 4.14] ( ) (The Hon. Mohamed Shafeek Rajabdeen) Bismillahir Rahmanir Raheem. Nahmaduhu Wa Nusalli Ala Rasoolihil Kareem Venerable Presiding Member, I thank you for giving me this opportunity to speak a few words on the Debate on the Vote on Account presented today which seeks the approval of the House to allocate sums required for the Government for the next four months. When you look at the First Schedule to the Vote on Account 2010, you would see that large sums of money have been

allocated to the Minister of Defence, Public Security, Law and Order, Sri Lanka Army, Sri Lanka Navy, Sri Lanka Air Force, Department of Police, Department of Civil Security and also to the Department of Coast Guard of Sri Lanka. Venerable Presiding Member, the reduction of interest rates has no bearing whatsoever on the Vote on Account presented today. I must frankly tell you that the colossal expenditure incurred by this Government without proper budgetary plans made you to bring in this Vote on Account. As you would see, people have not done their part properly. As the Hon. Karu Jayasuriya said, though the Ministry of Public Administration has been allocated a colossal amount of money, the level of work in that area has not been enhanced. When you take the City of Colombo, I, as a Member of the Sri Lanka Muslim Congress representing the Colombo District, wish to emphasize that though the Colombo Municipal Council has spent a lot of money on the roadways, we are in a pathetic situation. Some of the city roads have not been developed at all and some are being developed over and over again. If you look at Ward Place, there is no reason for them to spend money on an additional pavement. The roads in this country should be widened but now the roads are getting smaller and smaller. Who is handling the development of the roadway system in this country? Sometime ago, the roadways were reduced by about four feet on each side and today they are being widened a little. So, there is a colossal waste of public funds in these areas by the Government institutions. If you look at the Low Level Road from Colombo to Avissawella, for the last 30 years the Government has not implemented any programme to develop it. There is no drainage system from Wellampitiya to Kaduwela. Therefore, as a Member representing this area, I would say that the low level area has to be concentrated on. When you go round the country, you will see that the roads are carpeted very well, but the City of Colombo has not been given proper attention. It was once said, . . Venerable Presiding Member, I also want to speak about the barricades in the City of Colombo. Now that the war is over and His Excellency the President is moving around, the barricades must be removed forthwith. Barricades are a hindrance to the people to move in the City of Colombo where most of the business take place. If you look at Pettah, it has become a ghost town. All businesses there have come down; the business of small and medium-scale people have come down. When the Government does not channel enough resources to these areas, naturally the Government in office will not survive. The Government has not given any support whatsoever to the industries, especially to the small and medium-scale industries. With regard to the GSP Plus, there are six Ministers running around the world seeking GSP Plus concession. I understand that a delegation of priests is also now going

17 PL 004533 (2009/11)

259 260

with a begging bowl to the UN and to the European Union seeking GSP Plus concession. We are in a situation where this country is running into loss. I would tell the Hon. Susil Premajayantha, Minister of Education that as far as the education of this country is concerned, the level of education has come down. Education must be improved; adequate infrastructure, proper universities and proper accommodation must be given. Accommodation has been promised but infrastructure has not been provided. Many Ministers are talking about higher education. They are in a dream world; they are not talking about the reality. I want to invite the attention of the House to the role played by the Minister of Higher Education. He has a Deputy Minister but he is not able to work with him. When you ask the Deputy Minister, Can you do this?, he says, I have no office to work. So, this is a one-man show. I thought it is only the President who is running a one-man show. Of course, I appreciate the Government of Mahinda Rajapaksa, his work and his schedule. The war was won with the combined support of the armed forces. There are six Ministers for Nation Building. They waste a colossal amount of money. There is no long-term planning. There are roads and bridges that were built overnight but there is no assurance that those will survive for the next 20 years. ( ) (The Presiding Member)

Thank you. ( ) (The Hon. Mohamed Shafeek Rajabdeen)

Venerable Presiding Member, please give me one minute more. I would say that there are six Ministers for Nation Building and they are all under the direction of one individual, the Hon. Basil Rajapaksa, a relative of His Excellency the President. All Ministers look up to him for decision-making. This is a family work that is going on. Therefore, we would like to have an independent Minister who has a backbone to work properly and give the poor people of this country what is required. As a Member of the Sri Lanka Muslim Congress, I represent this august Assembly. We are here to speak on behalf of our people; we are not asking for power. We are sent here to speak on behalf of our people. My people are suffering; my businessmen are suffering. The City of Colombo is in the doldrums. So, I would kindly ask you to see that Colombo is properly maintained because this is a main city. I would once again say that most of the roads, the education sector and the business sector are neglected. You cannot develop the rural areas neglecting the urban areas.

In conclusion, I wish to thank you, Venerable Presiding Member, for giving me a few additional minutes to speak. ( ) (The Presiding Member) . . . . . . ( ) ( . . - ) (The Hon. S. M. Chandrasena - Minister of Nation Building) , " . . " . , . . Question put, and agreed to. () , . . . , (.) , .. . Whereupon THE HON. (VEN.) UDAWATTE NANDA THERO left the Chair, and THE HON. Y.M. NAVARATNE BANDA took the Chair.

( ) (The Presiding Member) . ( ) ( - ) (The Hon. Mano Wijeyeratne-Minister of Enterprise Development) , . . ( ) (The Presiding Member) . ( ) (The Hon. Mano Wijeyeratne) . ( ) (The Presiding Member) .

Subscriptions : The annual subscription for Official Report of Hansard is Rs. 2,178. A single copy of Hansard is available for Rs. 18.15. (Postage Rs. 2.50) Copies can be obtained by remitting in advance an annual subscription fee to the SUPERINTENDENT, GOVERNMENT PUBLICATIONS BUREAU, No. 132, Maya Avenue, Kirulapone, Colombo 5. The fee should reach him on or before November 30 each year . Late applications for subscriptions will not be accepted.
